TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: Each of the boys in the class | have submitted | their assignment | before the deadline | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 1
EXPLAIN: "Each" always takes a singular verb, so "have submitted" should be "has submitted".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The manager insisted that | both the clerk as well as the cashier | are responsible | for the missing cash | No error
ANSWER: C
RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: With "as well as", the verb agrees only with the first subject ("the clerk"), so it should be "is responsible".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: This is the officer | whom everybody says | will be transferred | to the Chennai branch | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 3
EXPLAIN: "Whom" is wrongly used, as it functions as the subject of "will be transferred"; it should be "who everybody says".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: If the bank had reduced | the interest rate earlier | more customers will apply | for home loans | No error
ANSWER: C
RULE: 4
EXPLAIN: The if-clause is in Past Perfect (Type III), so the main clause needs "would have applied", not "will apply".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: One of the reasons | for the delay in loan approval | are the incomplete documents | submitted by the applicant | No error
ANSWER: C
RULE: 5
EXPLAIN: "One of the + plural noun" as the subject (no relative pronoun) takes a singular verb, so it should be "is the incomplete documents".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The bank released | a two-hundred-crore | rupees loan | to the textile sector | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 6
EXPLAIN: In "Number + Unit + Noun", the unit stays singular, so "two-hundred-crore" is correct, but the compound should read "two-hundred-crore-rupee loan" â€” the unit "rupees" wrongly takes the plural before the noun "loan".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: He has been working | in this bank | since five years | and plans to retire soon | No error
ANSWER: C
RULE: 9
EXPLAIN: A point in time period is expressed with "for", not "since"; it should be "for five years".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: By the time the auditor arrived | the accountant already left | the office with all the files | in his bag | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 10
EXPLAIN: The earlier of two past actions needs the Past Perfect, so it should be "had already left".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The manager appreciated | me completing | the audit report | ahead of schedule | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 11
EXPLAIN: A possessive adjective, not an objective pronoun, should precede a gerund; it should be "my completing".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: Never before | the bank has witnessed | such a huge rush | of loan applicants | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 12
EXPLAIN: When a sentence begins with a negative adverb like "never", the Law of Inversion applies, so it should be "has the bank witnessed".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR

ANSWER: B
RULE: 13
EXPLAIN: Going to church for worship (its primary purpose) takes no article; it should be "goes to church every Sunday". (Part D is correct, since repairing the clock is a secondary purpose and takes "the".)
%%%

EXPLAIN: "Except" takes the objective case; it should be "except him".

EXPLAIN: No error â€” after the pseudo subject "it", the subjective case "I" is correctly used, matching the verb "am".
%%%

EXPLAIN: "Both...and" (not "both...nor") should be used, requiring a plural verb: "were present"; "nor" must be replaced with "and".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: If the auditor __will find__ any discrepancy, he will report it immediately.
OPTIONS: found | finds | had found | No improvement | will have found
ANSWER: B
RULE: 4
EXPLAIN: In a Type I conditional, the if-clause takes the Simple Present ("finds").
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: One of the reports that __was submitted__ late has been rejected by the auditor.
OPTIONS: were submitted | is submitted | has submitted | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 5
EXPLAIN: Since the relative pronoun "that" refers back to the plural "reports", the plural verb "were submitted" is needed.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: He has been living in this city __since ten years__.
OPTIONS: for ten years | since ten year | from ten years | No improvement
ANSWER: B
RULE: 9
EXPLAIN: A duration of time takes "for", not "since".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: After the accountant __had left__ the office, the auditor arrived to check the ledgers.
OPTIONS: has left | left | leaves | No improvement
ANSWER: D
RULE: 10
EXPLAIN: No improvement needed â€” the earlier action correctly uses the Past Perfect "had left".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The manager appreciated __me completing__ the audit report ahead of schedule.
OPTIONS: my completing | I completing | myself completing | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 11
EXPLAIN: A possessive adjective should be used before a gerund: "my completing".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __The report along with the annexures were sent__ to the regional office yesterday.
OPTIONS: The report along with the annexures was sent | The report along with the annexures have been sent | The reports along with the annexure were sent | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: With "along with", the verb agrees only with the first (singular) subject, "the report".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The clerk __who I believe__ will be transferred is sitting right there.
OPTIONS: whom I believe | who I believes | whom does I believe | No improvement
ANSWER: D
RULE: 3
EXPLAIN: No improvement needed â€” "who" is correctly used as the subject of "will be transferred".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __Never before the bank has witnessed__ such a huge rush of loan applicants.
OPTIONS: Never before has the bank witnessed | Never before the bank had witnessed | Never the bank has witnessed before | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 12
EXPLAIN: A sentence beginning with a negative adverb requires inversion: helping verb before the subject.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __Hardly had the meeting begun than__ the power went off.
OPTIONS: Hardly had the meeting begun when | Hardly the meeting had begun than | Hardly did the meeting begin than | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 14
EXPLAIN: "Hardly" is always followed by "when", never "than".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The new intern __availed the opportunity__ to work on live client projects.
OPTIONS: availed himself of the opportunity | availed of himself the opportunity | availed himself the opportunity of | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 15
EXPLAIN: "Avail" must be followed by a reflexive pronoun and "of": "availed himself of the opportunity".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The five business partners __always support each other__ in every major decision.
OPTIONS: always support one another | always supports each other | always support themselves | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 22
EXPLAIN: Since there are more than two partners, "one another" should replace "each other".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: This is __very best scheme__ offered by the bank this festive season.
OPTIONS: the very best scheme | very the best scheme | much the best scheme | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "Very" with a superlative must be preceded by "the".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __Although the market crashed but__ the fund manager remained calm throughout the day.
OPTIONS: Although the market crashed | Although the market has crashed but | Because the market crashed but | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 27
EXPLAIN: "Although" never takes "but" in the main clause; "but" should simply be dropped.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: I have __already submit__ my resignation letter to the HR department.
OPTIONS: already submitted | already submits | already submitting | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 29
EXPLAIN: "Already" is used with the Perfect Tense, requiring "submitted".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: His careless attitude __is injurious for__ his career in the long run.
OPTIONS: is injurious to | is injurious with | is injurious of | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 31
EXPLAIN: "Injurious" is always followed by "to".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: This building __is three times larger than__ the old branch office.
OPTIONS: is three times as large as | is three times more large than | is thrice times larger than | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 33
EXPLAIN: "Times" is never followed by a comparative degree; it should pair with "as...as".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The teacher asked the students __that why they__ had not submitted the assignment.
OPTIONS: why they | that they why | why did they | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 34
EXPLAIN: An indirect question should follow statement word order without "that" preceding the question word.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: Of the two schemes, this one is __more profitabler__ than the other.
OPTIONS: more profitable | much profitable | profitabler | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 36
EXPLAIN: A double comparative is incorrect; "more profitable" is the correct form.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: She has __little knowledge__ about few important banking terms used in the exam.
OPTIONS: a little knowledge about a few important banking terms | little knowledge about a little important banking terms | a few knowledge about few banking terms | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 40
EXPLAIN: "Knowledge" (uncountable) needs "a little" for a small positive amount, and "banking terms" (countable) needs "a few" to mean "some".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: Kindly __return back__ the loan documents at the earliest possible time.
OPTIONS: return | send back | revert back | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 43
EXPLAIN: "Return" already implies "back", so the redundant word should be dropped.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __The table's leg__ was broken during the office shifting last week.
OPTIONS: The leg of the table | The leg of table | Table's the leg | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 44
EXPLAIN: Non-living things generally use "of" instead of the possessive apostrophe.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: This is __the most perfect__ solution to the ongoing fraud problem.
OPTIONS: the perfect | the most perfectest | very perfect | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 46
EXPLAIN: "Perfect" is an absolute adjective and cannot take "most".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: He was __quite all satisfied__ with the settlement offered by the company.
OPTIONS: quite satisfied | all quite satisfied | quite all so satisfied | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 47
EXPLAIN: "Quite" and "all" cannot be used together in the same sentence.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: A number of customers __has complained__ about the new mobile banking app.
OPTIONS: have complained | has complain | having complained | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 51
EXPLAIN: "A number of + plural noun" takes a plural verb.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: It is high time the government __takes strict action__ against loan defaulters.
OPTIONS: took strict action | will take strict action | has taken strict action | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 52
EXPLAIN: "It is high time" directly followed by a subject takes the past tense form.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: I don't know __to solve__ this reconciliation problem at all.
OPTIONS: how to solve | for solving | to solving | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 54
EXPLAIN: "Know" is never directly followed by "to"; a wh-word such as "how" is required.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: He would rather resign __than to accept__ this humiliating transfer.
OPTIONS: than accept | than to accepting | rather than accepting | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 55
EXPLAIN: "Rather" is followed by "than + base verb", without "to".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The officer could not __help to notice__ the discrepancy in the ledger.
OPTIONS: help noticing | help to noticing | help notice | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 60
EXPLAIN: "Help" in this sense takes "V1+ing" (a gerund), not "to + V1".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: She is __a honest and hardworking__ employee of the bank.
OPTIONS: an honest and hardworking | an honesty and hardworking | a honesty and hardworking | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 61
EXPLAIN: "Honest" starts with a vowel sound (silent h), so it takes "an".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word most nearly SIMILAR in meaning to "PRUDENT" (as often asked in banking vocabulary sections).
OPTIONS: careless | wise | reckless | ignorant
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Prudent" means acting with careful judgement, i.e. wise or sensible.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word OPPOSITE in meaning to "AUSTERITY", often used in RBI monetary policy articles.
OPTIONS: frugality | extravagance | simplicity | restraint
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Austerity" means strict economy/simple living; its opposite is "extravagance".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Select the correct ONE-WORD SUBSTITUTION for "a person who lends money at a very high rate of interest".
OPTIONS: banker | usurer | creditor | financier
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: A "usurer" is one who lends money at an excessively high (illegal) interest rate.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Select the correct ONE-WORD SUBSTITUTION for "a document by which a person states how his property is to be disposed of after death".
OPTIONS: affidavit | will | deed | mandate
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: A "will" is a legal document stating how one's property should be distributed after death.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the correctly spelt word.
OPTIONS: Recieve | Acheive | Occurrence | Concious
ANSWER: C
EXPLAIN: "Occurrence" is spelt correctly; the others should be "Receive", "Achieve", and "Conscious".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the correctly spelt word (a frequent spot-the-correctly-spelt-word item in IBPS Clerk prelims).
OPTIONS: Entreprenuer | Entrepreneur | Enterpreneur | Entreprenur
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Entrepreneur" is the correct spelling.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word most nearly OPPOSITE in meaning to "LIABILITY" in a banking/finance context.
OPTIONS: debt | asset | loan | deficit
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: In finance, "liability" (what is owed) is opposite to "asset" (what is owned).
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Select the correct ONE-WORD SUBSTITUTION for "money paid back for something already paid".
OPTIONS: rebate | refund | reimbursement | discount
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: A "refund" is money returned for an amount already paid.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The very safeguards meant to prevent such fraud | was rendered | useless | by an outdated software system | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "The very safeguards" is plural; it should be "were rendered useless".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: The two rival bidders, either of whom ____ to gain significantly, ____ lobbied hard for regulatory approval.
OPTIONS: stand / has | stands / have | stands / has | stand / have
ANSWER: C
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Either of whom" (within its clause) takes a singular verb ("stands"), and "the two rival bidders" (main subject, plural) takes "have lobbied".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Neither of the two whistleblowers, who had risked everything to expose the fraud, ____ given adequate protection ____ the authorities afterward.
OPTIONS: was / by | were / by | was / from | were / from
ANSWER: A
RULE: 114, 58
EXPLAIN: "Neither of" takes a singular verb ("was given"), and "by" is used for the living agent providing (or failing to provide) protection.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The clerk's negligence, coupled with the manager's oversight, | were responsible | for the discrepancy | that went unnoticed for months | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: "Coupled with" ties the verb to the singular first subject "the clerk's negligence"; it should be "was responsible".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: More than one scheme have been | withdrawn | after the regulator | flagged irregularities in disbursement | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 37
EXPLAIN: "More than one" takes a singular verb; it should be "has been withdrawn".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: Neither the auditors nor the compliance officer __were able to explain__ the sudden discrepancy in the books.
OPTIONS: was able to explain | was able for explaining | were able for explain | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 35
EXPLAIN: With "neither/nor", the verb agrees with the nearer subject "the compliance officer" (singular), requiring "was able".
%%%
TYPE: MATCH
Q: Match the idioms with their correct meanings.
LEFT: 1. Skeleton in the closet | 2. Smoke and mirrors | 3. Paper trail
RIGHT: P. A documented record of transactions used as evidence | Q. A hidden, embarrassing secret from the past | R. Deceptive or misleading explanations that obscure the truth
OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R
ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Skeleton in the closet" = hidden secret; "smoke and mirrors" = deceptive obfuscation; "paper trail" = documented evidence.
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the regional offices, despite operating under the same guidelines, ____ the compliance rules ____ from one another.
OPTIONS: interpret / differently | interprets / differently | interpret / different | interprets / different
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114, 103
EXPLAIN: "Each of the regional offices" takes a singular verb ("interprets"), and "differently" (adverb, not adjective) correctly modifies the verb.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Select the correct ONE-WORD SUBSTITUTION for "a person appointed to manage the affairs of a company that is in financial difficulty".
OPTIONS: trustee | receiver | executor | custodian
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: A "receiver" is appointed to manage a company's assets during insolvency proceedings.
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

OPTIONS: takes / will suffer | took / should suffer | will take / suffer | had taken / suffered
ANSWER: B
RULE: 52, 78
EXPLAIN: "It is high time" takes the past tense form ("took"), and "lest" is followed by "should".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

OPTIONS: was / went | were / went | was / had gone | were / had gone

RULE: 35
EXPLAIN: With "not only...but also", the verb agrees with the nearer subject "subordinates" (plural): "were held" and "went unnoticed".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: The manager, ____ his two deputies, ____ made to sit through a lengthy compliance training that lasted nearly five hours.
OPTIONS: as well as / was | as well as / were | along with / were | together with / have
ANSWER: A
RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: "As well as" ties the verb to the singular first subject "the manager", requiring "was made".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word most nearly SIMILAR in meaning to "CULPABLE", as used when assigning blame in a bank fraud case.
OPTIONS: innocent | blameworthy | exempt | vindicated

EXPLAIN: "Culpable" means deserving blame, similar to "blameworthy".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

ANSWER: B

EXPLAIN: "Involvement" in this sense is uncountable and takes no plural form.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word OPPOSITE in meaning to "MALFEASANCE", a term often used regarding official misconduct.
OPTIONS: wrongdoing | corruption | integrity | dishonesty
ANSWER: C
EXPLAIN: "Malfeasance" (official wrongdoing) is opposite to "integrity" (honesty, moral uprightness).
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The auditor's findings, together with the whistleblower's testimony, | was enough | to trigger | a full-scale regulatory investigation | No error
ANSWER: B

EXPLAIN: "Together with" ties the verb to the plural first subject "the auditor's findings"; it should be "were enough".
%%%

ANSWER: C
RULE: 18, 4
EXPLAIN: "Effecting" (to bring about) is confused with "affecting" (to influence); it should be "affecting thousands of small investors".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR

ANSWER: B
RULE: 12, 20
EXPLAIN: "Who" is correctly used as the subject of the following clause, but since it follows "trusted" as an object here, it should be "whom they trusted completely".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT

EXPLAIN: "The very fact" is singular, requiring "speaks volumes".
%%%

RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: "As well as" keeps the verb tied to the first (singular) subject "the manager"; it should be "was made".
%%%

EXPLAIN: "None of" traditionally takes a singular verb in formal exam grammar; it should be "was willing to disclose".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

%%%

EXPLAIN: The pseudo subject construction "It was...who" requires the verb to match the singular emphasised subject; it should be "who was quoted".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ

OPTIONS: genuine | apparent | concealed | verified
ANSWER: B

%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

%%%
TYPE: MATCH

RIGHT: P. A brief, temporary recovery in falling prices | Q. A rising market | R. An aggressive takeover offer at a very high premium
OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R

%%%

%%%
TYPE: MCQ

%%%

%%%

%%%

ANSWER: E

%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly combines the "a series/batch/string of" singular-agreement rule with the correct preposition?
OPTIONS: A string of complaints against the branch were filed with the ombudsman | A string of complaints against the branch was filed with the ombudsman | A string of complaints against the branch was filed to the ombudsman | A string of complaints against the branch were filed to the ombudsman

EXPLAIN: "A string of" is treated as singular ("was filed"), and "filed with" is the correct idiomatic preposition for an ombudsman.

%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The two whistleblowers, each of whom risked their careers, | was later | commended | by the regulatory authority | No error

PARTS: The complaint, along with supporting documents, | were forwarded | to the ombudsman | for further investigation | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 17
EXPLAIN: "Along with" ties the verb to the singular "the complaint"; it should be "was forwarded".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Neither of the two accountants, who joined only last month, ____ aware that the software ____ already flagged the anomaly.
OPTIONS: was / had | were / had | was / has | were / has
ANSWER: A
RULE: 114, 10
EXPLAIN: "Neither of" takes a singular verb ("was"), and the earlier action of flagging needs the Past Perfect ("had already flagged").
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: The two directors, ____ the board suspects of embezzlement, ____ been asked to resign with immediate effect.
OPTIONS: who / has | whom / have | who / have | whom / has
ANSWER: B
RULE: 20, 49
EXPLAIN: "Whom" is the object of "suspects", and since "the two directors" is plural, it should be "have been asked".
%%%
TYPE: MATCH
Q: Match the idioms with their correct meanings.
LEFT: 1. Bailout | 2. Haircut (financial) | 3. Fire sale
RIGHT: P. Selling assets quickly and cheaply, often under distress | Q. Financial rescue of a failing entity, often by the government | R. A reduction in the value or repayment of a debt
OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R
ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Bailout" = financial rescue; "haircut" = reduced repayment value; "fire sale" = distressed quick sale of assets.

TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly combines the "neither...nor" rule with the correct use of "beside/besides"?
OPTIONS: Besides the CFO, neither the auditors nor the compliance head was informed in time | Beside the CFO, neither the auditors nor the compliance head were informed in time | Besides the CFO, neither the auditors nor the compliance head were informed in time | Beside the CFO, neither the auditors nor the compliance head was informed in time
ANSWER: A
RULE: 35, 102
EXPLAIN: "Besides" (in addition to) fits the sense of excluding the CFO from those uninformed, and the verb agrees with the nearer subject "the compliance head" (singular).

ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Sweat equity" = value from labour; "golden parachute" = executive departure package; "vested interest" = personal stake in an outcome.

ANSWER: A

OPTIONS: He sat beside her; besides, he also paid the bill | He sat besides her; beside, he also paid the bill | He sat beside her; beside, he also paid the bill | He sat besides her; besides, he also paid the bill
ANSWER: A
RULE: 102
EXPLAIN: "Beside" means "next to", and "besides" means "in addition to" â€” this option uses each correctly.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly uses "fewer" and "less"?
OPTIONS: There are less customers today, so there is fewer rush | There are fewer customers today, so there is less rush | There is fewer customers today, so there are less rush | There are fewer customer today, so there is less rushes
ANSWER: B
RULE: 111
EXPLAIN: "Fewer" is used with the countable noun "customers", and "less" is used with the uncountable noun "rush".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which of the following uses "each other" and "one another" correctly?
OPTIONS: The two partners always help one another; the five directors respect each other | The two partners always help each other; the five directors respect one another | The two partners always help each other; the five directors respect each other | The two partners always help one another; the five directors respect one another
ANSWER: B
RULE: 22
EXPLAIN: "Each other" suits two partners, while "one another" suits the five directors (more than two).
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the option that correctly distinguishes "affect" and "effect".
OPTIONS: The new policy will affect small businesses; its effect will be felt for years | The new policy will effect small businesses; its affect will be felt for years | The new policy will affect small businesses; its affect will be felt for years | The new policy will effect small businesses; its effect will be felt for years, and affect it more
ANSWER: A
RULE: 18
EXPLAIN: "Affect" is a verb (to influence), and "effect" is a noun (the result).
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Select the correct ONE-WORD SUBSTITUTION for "one who is unable to pay one's debt".
OPTIONS: debtor | defaulter | insolvent | creditor
ANSWER: C
EXPLAIN: "Insolvent" specifically means one who is unable to pay debts.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ

%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word OPPOSITE in meaning to "TRANSPARENT" as used in "transparent lending practices".
OPTIONS: clear | obscure | evident | candid
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Transparent" (open, clear) is opposite to "obscure" (unclear, hidden).
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly demonstrates the "male/female vs man/woman" rule?
OPTIONS: The zoo has a female tiger; the bank hired a woman manager | The zoo has a woman tiger; the bank hired a female manager | The zoo has a female tiger; the bank hired a female manager | The zoo has a male tiger; the bank hired a man manager for the ladies' branch
ANSWER: A
RULE: 67
EXPLAIN: "Female" correctly describes the tiger's characteristic, and "woman" correctly describes the manager's role.
%%%

ANSWER: B

TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which option correctly uses "elder" and "older"?
OPTIONS: My elder brother is older than my neighbour's son | My older brother is elder than my neighbour's son | My elder brother is elder than my neighbour's son | My older brother is older than my neighbour's son, who is my elder
ANSWER: A
RULE: 112
EXPLAIN: "Elder" is used within the family ("elder brother"), and "older" compares age with someone outside the family.

%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly uses "beside" vs. "besides" AND "farther" vs. "further" together?
OPTIONS: Besides the manager, no one sat farther from the desk; further discussion followed | Beside the manager, no one sat further from the desk; besides discussion followed | Besides the manager, no one sat further from the desk; farther discussion followed | Beside the manager, no one sat farther from the desk; further discussion followed
ANSWER: D
RULE: 102
EXPLAIN: "Beside" (next to) fits the seating position, "farther" fits physical distance, and "further" (additional) fits the discussion.

TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the two pending mergers awaiting regulatory clearance ____ uncertain prospects ____ the ongoing scrutiny.
OPTIONS: face / amid | faces / amid | face / among | faces / among
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two pending mergers" takes a singular verb ("faces"), and "amid" (for an ongoing situation) fits better than "among" (for countable items).
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

ANSWER: B
RULE: 114, 49
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two auditors' conclusions" takes a singular verb ("leaves"), and "uncertain about" is the correct preposition.
%%%

Q: The very safeguards the RBI introduced last year, ironically, __has failed to prevent__ this fresh round of NPA accumulation.
OPTIONS: have failed to prevent | has failed for preventing | have failed for prevent | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "The very safeguards" is plural, requiring "have failed".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: Neither the compliance head nor the risk officers __was consulted before__ the decision was finalised.
OPTIONS: were consulted before | was consult before | were consult before | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 35
EXPLAIN: The verb agrees with the nearer subject "the risk officers" (plural), requiring "were consulted".

Banking English â€” Hard / Extreme-Hard Practice Set â€” PART 3 (72 Questions)
SBI PO Mains / IBPS PO Mains level difficulty
Question types randomly mixed: Spot Error, Fill in the Blank, Sentence Improvement, Vocabulary/Grammar MCQ, Match the Following
Most questions combine 2 (occasionally 3) grammar rules from your 120-rule list â€” the RULE field lists all rules involved
Running total so far: Part 1 (350) + Part 2 (129) + Part 3 (72) = 551 of 1000

TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the two competing offers for the stressed asset ____ at the end ____ this week.
OPTIONS: expire / of | expires / of | expire / at | expires / at
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two competing offers" takes a singular verb ("expires"), and "at the end of" is the correct fixed phrase.
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the two audit committees formed after the scandal ____ under entirely different reporting ____.
OPTIONS: operate / structures | operates / structures | operate / structure | operates / structure
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two audit committees" takes a singular verb ("operates").
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The very testimony that convicted the accountant | were later | recanted | under mysterious circumstances | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "The very testimony" is singular; it should be "was later recanted under mysterious circumstances".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Identify the sentence that correctly combines "a committee/battalion/regiment of" singular agreement with the correct possessive.
OPTIONS: A committee of experts submitted their report on time | A committee of experts submitted its report on time | A committee of expert submitted its report on time | A committee of experts submitted it's report on time
ANSWER: B
RULE: 30
EXPLAIN: The committee acts as a single unit, requiring the singular possessive "its report".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: The goods stored in the bonded warehouse, pending customs clearance, ____ later found to be ____.
OPTIONS: was / counterfeit | were / counterfeit | was / counterfeits | were / counterfeits
ANSWER: B
RULE: 92
EXPLAIN: "Goods" is always plural, requiring "were later found".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: A herd of small investors, lured by promises of guaranteed returns, | were left | with nothing | after the scheme collapsed | No error
ANSWER: E
RULE: 30
EXPLAIN: No error â€” since the investors were affected individually and diversely, "were left" (plural) correctly agrees with the collective noun "herd" used here figuratively.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The very promotion that the branch manager had been denied twice before | were finally | granted | after his transfer to the corporate office | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "The very promotion" is singular; it should be "was finally granted".

ANSWER: B

EXPLAIN: "Each of the two competing valuations" takes a singular verb; it should be "differs by nearly thirty percent".

TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the two contradicting witnesses, both employees of the accused firm, ____ later found to have perjured ____.
OPTIONS: was / themselves | were / themselves | was / itself | were / itself
ANSWER: A
RULE: 114, 15
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two contradicting witnesses" takes a singular verb ("was found"), while "themselves" is retained as the natural reflexive for a plural-implying "witnesses" construction.

TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly combines "each of the two" agreement with the correct form of "differ from"?
OPTIONS: Each of the two contracts differ from the standard template significantly | Each of the two contracts differs from the standard template significantly | Each of the two contracts differs with the standard template significantly | Each of the two contracts differ with the standard template significantly
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114, 81
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two contracts" takes a singular verb ("differs"), and "differ from" (not "with") is the correct idiomatic preposition.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The winnings from the fraudulent lottery scheme, distributed among several accomplices, | was eventually | traced | and confiscated | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 92
EXPLAIN: "Winnings" is always plural; it should be "were eventually traced and confiscated".

PARTS: The very reforms promised during the election campaign | was never | implemented | despite repeated public demand | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 24
EXPLAIN: "The very reforms" is plural; it should be "were never implemented".

TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Each of the two competing valuations of the distressed asset ____ by nearly thirty ____.
OPTIONS: differ / percent | differs / percent | differ / percentage | differs / percentage
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two competing valuations" takes a singular verb ("differs"), and "percent" (not "percentage") is used with a specific number.

TYPE: MATCH
Q: Match the idioms with their correct meanings.
LEFT: 1. Cut and run | 2. Above suspicion | 3. Caught red-handed
RIGHT: P. Discovered in the act of doing something wrong | Q. To abandon a situation abruptly to avoid loss | R. Considered entirely trustworthy and beyond doubt
OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R
ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Cut and run" = abandon abruptly; "above suspicion" = beyond doubt; "caught red-handed" = caught in the act.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: Each of the two forged wills presented in court | claim | to be | the genuine final testament | No error
ANSWER: B
RULE: 114
EXPLAIN: "Each of the two forged wills" takes a singular verb; it should be "claims to be the genuine final testament".
%%%
TYPE: MATCH
Q: Match the idioms with their correct meanings.
LEFT: 1. Hush money | 2. Kickback | 3. Grease someone's palm
RIGHT: P. An illicit payment made to secure favourable treatment | Q. Money paid to keep someone silent about wrongdoing | R. A portion of illicit profit returned to someone who facilitated a deal
OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R
ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Hush money" = payment for silence; "kickback" = illicit share of profit; "grease someone's palm" = bribe someone.
%%%
TYPE: MATCH
Q: Match the idioms with their correct meanings.
LEFT: 1. Deep-six a deal | 2. Get cold feet | 3. Sign on the dotted line
RIGHT: P. To become nervous and hesitant about proceeding with a plan | Q. To formally finalise an agreement | R. To abandon or kill a deal deliberately
OPTIONS: 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-R, 2-Q, 3-P
ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Deep-six a deal" = kill it deliberately; "get cold feet" = become hesitant; "sign on the dotted line" = finalise an agreement.
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word OPPOSITE in meaning to "EXONERATION", as used when a suspect is cleared of charges.
OPTIONS: acquittal | vindication | conviction | absolution
ANSWER: C
EXPLAIN: "Exoneration" (being cleared of blame) is opposite to "conviction" (being found guilty).

Q: Choose the word most nearly SIMILAR in meaning to "VENAL", as used to describe a corrupt official accepting bribes.
OPTIONS: incorruptible | mercenary | honest | dutiful

EXPLAIN: "Venal" means susceptible to bribery, similar to "mercenary" (motivated by money).

OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R

OPTIONS: 1-Q, 2-R, 3-P | 1-P, 2-Q, 3-R | 1-R, 2-P, 3-Q | 1-Q, 2-P, 3-R

Banking English â€” Hard / Extreme-Hard Practice Set â€” PART 4 (102 Questions)
SBI PO Mains / IBPS PO Mains level difficulty
Question types randomly mixed: Spot Error, Fill in the Blank, Sentence Improvement, Vocabulary/Grammar MCQ, Match the Following
Most questions combine 2 (occasionally 3) grammar rules from your 120-rule list â€” the RULE field lists all rules involved
Running total so far: Part 1 (350) + Part 2 (129) + Part 3 (72) + Part 4 (102) = 653 of 1000

TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: This scheme attracts __five times more investors__ than the earlier one launched last year.
OPTIONS: five times as many investors as | five times more investors as | as five times investors than | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 33
EXPLAIN: "Times" cannot be followed by a comparative degree; it should pair with "as many...as".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: He is one of those officers who never misses | a single deadline, | however tight | the schedule may be | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 5
EXPLAIN: The relative pronoun "who" refers to the plural "officers", requiring a plural verb; it should be "who never miss a single deadline".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word most nearly SIMILAR in meaning to "PERFUNCTORY", as in "a perfunctory review of the accounts".
OPTIONS: thorough | careless and hasty | meticulous | exhaustive
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Perfunctory" means done without care or interest, merely as a routine duty.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: Somebody else's signature | appeared | on the fraudulent | withdrawal slip | No error
ANSWER: E
RULE: 118
EXPLAIN: No error â€” "else's" is the correct possessive form, an exception that keeps the "s" despite the hissing sound.
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: Until the auditor completes the review, the branch cannot resume normal cash ____.
OPTIONS: operation | operations | operating | operate
ANSWER: B
RULE: 79
EXPLAIN: "Operations" (plural, referring to ongoing activities) fits naturally with "resume", and "until" correctly relates the time-based condition.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The old cashier died from a heart condition | that he had | been suffering | from for over a decade | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 101
EXPLAIN: "Die of" is used for a disease/ailment, not "die from"; it should be "died of a heart condition".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Identify the sentence that correctly applies the "between...and" rule alongside the correct objective case.
OPTIONS: The dispute is strictly between him and I | The dispute is strictly between he and me | The dispute is strictly between him and me | The dispute is strictly between he and I
ANSWER: C
RULE: 107, 41
EXPLAIN: "Between" is followed by "and" (not "to"), and both pronouns take the objective case.
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK

OPTIONS: also / to | too / at | also / at | too / to
ANSWER: A
RULE: 104, 87
EXPLAIN: "Also" is correctly placed before the verb here (not between the verb and object), and "to the branch manager" is the correct preposition.

%%%

EXPLAIN: An indirect yes/no question is introduced by "whether" alone (without "that"), and "yet" fits the pending-action sense.

ANSWER: A

TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __It was them__ who first noticed the discrepancy in the ledger.
OPTIONS: It was they | It was theirs | It were them | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 116
EXPLAIN: After the pseudo subject "it was", the subjective case is required: "It was they".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: This is the most efficient of the two systems | that the bank | has ever | implemented across branches | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 62
EXPLAIN: When comparing exactly two things, the comparative "the more efficient" is used, not the superlative "the most efficient".
%%%

ANSWER: A
RULE: 119
EXPLAIN: Possessive pronouns never take an apostrophe; it should be "This cheque is hers".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Which sentence correctly combines the "die of/die from" rule with the "collective noun" agreement rule?
OPTIONS: The entire team was shocked when their colleague died of a rare illness | The entire team were shocked when their colleague died from a rare illness | The entire team was shocked when their colleague died from a rare illness | The entire team were shocked when their colleague died of a rare illness
ANSWER: A
RULE: 30, 101
EXPLAIN: The team, acting as one shocked unit, takes "was", and "died of a rare illness" correctly uses "of" for a disease.
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: Both directors' signatures | were required | on the cheque | before it could be processed | No error

TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: This scheme attracts __five times more investors__ than the earlier one launched last year.
OPTIONS: five times as many investors as | five times more investors as | as five times investors than | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 33
EXPLAIN: "Times" cannot be followed by a comparative degree; it should pair with "as many...as".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: He is one of those officers who never misses | a single deadline, | however tight | the schedule may be | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 5
EXPLAIN: The relative pronoun "who" refers to the plural "officers", requiring a plural verb; it should be "who never miss a single deadline".
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word most nearly SIMILAR in meaning to "PERFUNCTORY", as in "a perfunctory review of the accounts".
OPTIONS: thorough | careless and hasty | meticulous | exhaustive
ANSWER: B
EXPLAIN: "Perfunctory" means done without care or interest, merely as a routine duty.
%%%

EXPLAIN: After a verb of insistence like "insisted that", the subjunctive base form "submit" is used.
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: __Scarcely the news had broken out__ when panic spread across the entire trading floor.
OPTIONS: Scarcely had the news broken out | Scarcely the news broken out had | Scarcely did the news broke out | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 14
EXPLAIN: "Scarcely" triggers inversion, requiring the helping verb before the subject.

Banking English â€” Hard / Extreme-Hard Practice Set â€” PART 6 (62 Questions)
SBI PO Mains / IBPS PO Mains level difficulty
Question types randomly mixed: Spot Error, Fill in the Blank, Sentence Improvement, Vocabulary/Grammar MCQ, Match the Following
This part focuses heavily on commonly confused word pairs (affect/effect, principal/principle, stationary/stationery, etc.) plus subjunctive mood constructions
Running total so far: Part 1 (350) + Part 2 (129) + Part 3 (72) + Part 4 (102) + Part 5 (74) + Part 6 (62) = 789 of 1000

TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The company's moral was low | after | the second round | of layoffs this year | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 18
EXPLAIN: "Moral" (relating to ethics) is confused with "morale" (a sense of confidence/enthusiasm); it should be "The company's morale was low".
%%%
TYPE: FILL_BLANK
Q: The company's ____ was low after the second round of ____ this year.
OPTIONS: moral / layoffs | morale / layoffs | moral / layoff | morale / layoff
ANSWER: B
RULE: 18
EXPLAIN: "Morale" (confidence/spirit) is correct, not "moral" (relating to ethics).
%%%
TYPE: MCQ
Q: Identify the sentence that correctly combines "principal/principle" with the correct subjunctive form after "recommend that".
OPTIONS: The committee recommends that the principal amount be repaid first | The committee recommends that the principle amount is repaid first | The committee recommends that the principal amount is repaid first | The committee recommends that the principle amount be repaid first
ANSWER: A
RULE: 18, 34
EXPLAIN: "Principal" (sum of money) is correct, and "be repaid" (subjunctive base form) follows "recommends that".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The new circular will effect | all existing loan accounts | starting | from next month | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 18, 59
EXPLAIN: "Effect" (to bring about) is confused with "affect" (to influence); it should be "will affect all existing loan accounts", and "starting from" should more precisely read "starting next month" or "with effect from next month".
%%%
TYPE: SPOT_ERROR
PARTS: The bank could not precede | with the transaction | without proper | identification documents | No error
ANSWER: A
RULE: 18
EXPLAIN: "Precede" (to come before) is confused with "proceed" (to continue); it should be "could not proceed with the transaction".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT
Q: The bank decided to __loose the collateral requirement__ for small business loans.

TYPE: MCQ

ANSWER: A

EXPLAIN: "More than one" always takes a singular verb ("was drafted"), and "ambiguously" (adverb) modifies the verb.

TYPE: MCQ

EXPLAIN: "Ram's and Shyam's shares" (split possession, each owning separate shares) is plural, requiring "were recently revalued".

ANSWER: A
EXPLAIN: "Out-of-court settlement" = private agreement; "open-and-shut case" = obviously clear case; "hung jury" = deadlocked jury.

TYPE: MCQ
Q: Choose the word OPPOSITE in meaning to "ABROGATE", as in "the new law abrogates the earlier tax exemption".
OPTIONS: repeal | annul | establish | rescind
ANSWER: C
EXPLAIN: "Abrogate" (to repeal or cancel) is opposite to "establish".
%%%
TYPE: IMPROVEMENT

OPTIONS: submit their compliance certificates | submits its compliance certificate | submitted their compliance certificates | No improvement
ANSWER: A
RULE: 34
EXPLAIN: After "requires that", the subjunctive base form "submit" is used.
